Key Takeaway
The Sunni position affirms that God has attributes of meaning, and the Mu'tazila's denial is linguistically and rationally flawed because capability necessarily implies power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If the word 'capable' loses its meaning without power, what does it say about your own understanding of God when you attribute something to Him without the necessary implications? Will you challenge yourself to accept all that the revealed terms entail, even when it confronts your reason?

The Divine Attribute of Life: Definition and Proof
Commentary defining life and proving its necessity for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological definition of God's attribute of life, how it is distinguished from created life, and the rational proof for why God must possess life.

Core Idea
Life is a foundational divine attribute that makes all other attributes possible.

This lesson examines the divine attribute of life as presented by al-Sanusi. The commentator explains that life is the attribute that enables perception and other attributes. He distinguishes between eternal life (God's) and originated life (creation), and provides a logical proof that God must have life because He possesses power, will, and knowledge. Let's explore these concepts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the full literal translation to get the flow.
The passage includes a poem fragment, definitions, and a proof.
2
Understand the general definition of life
Notice that al-Sanusi defines life as 'an attribute that renders valid perception.' This is a broad definition covering both eternal and created life.
The commentator notes this is a 'rasm' (descriptive definition), not a strict logical definition.
3
Distinguish eternal life from originated life
Eternal life is defined as an attribute that necessitates the validity of knowledge (and other attributes). Originated life is defined as a quality that necessitates sensation and voluntary movement.
The word 'validity' is important: life makes knowledge possible, but does not automatically give knowledge (e.g., the insane person is alive but lacks knowledge).
4
Follow the logical proof
The proof is a syllogism: God has power, will, and knowledge. Everything with these attributes must have life. Therefore, God has life.
This is a straightforward deductive argument based on the necessary connection between certain attributes.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why life is a condition for other attributes: it is the foundation that makes perception and action possible, but it is not identical to them.
God's life is by His essence, not a spirit, unlike created life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حيَاتُهُ كَذَا الكَلامُ السَّمْعُ ثُمَّ البَصَرْ بِذِي أَتَانَا السَّمْـ
قوله : (حَيَاتُهُ) معطوف على الوجود بحذف حرف العطف، وما صنعه الشارح حل معنى كما تقدَّم، وقد عرف الشيخ السنوسي الحياة بتعريف يشمل الحياة القديمة والحادثة؛ حيث قال: هي صفةٌ تصحُحُ لمن قامت به الإدراك؛ أي: تصحح لمن قامت به أن يتصف بصفات الإدراك ) ، ولا يضره الجمع بين حقيقتين مختلفتين بالقدم والحدوث؛ لأنَّه رسم لا حد.
وعرف بعضهم منهما بتعريف يخصه، فعرف الحياة القديمة بقوله : (صفة أزلية تقتضي صحة العلم؛ أي: تقتضي صحة الاتصاف به وكما تقتضي صحة الاتصاف بالعلم تقتضي صحة الاتصاف بغيره من الصفات الواجبة، وإنما اقتصر على العلم لأنه شرط في غيره، وشرط الشرط شرط.
وأقحم (۲) لفظة (صحة) ؛ لأن الحياة لا تستلزم العلم بالفعل، لكن العلم واجب في حقه تعالى للدليل السابق وأما في حقنا فقد ينتفي العلم مع وجود الحياة، كما في المجنون؛ فإنه حي مع انتفاء العلم عنه .
وعرف الحياة الحادثة بقوله : (هي كيفية يلزمها قبول الحس والحركة الإرادية)؛ أي : عَرَضُ يلزمه قبول الإحساس وقبول الحركة الإرادية، بخلاف الحركة الاضطرارية كحركة الحجر بحركة محركه، وحياة الله لذاته ليست بروح، وحياتنا ليست لذاتنا بل بسبب روح
ودليل وجوب الحياة له تعالى أن تقول : الله متصف بالقدرة والإرادة والعلم، وكلُّ من كان كذلك تجب له الحياة، فالله تجب له الحياة.
(۱) قوله : (أي: تصحح لمن قامت به أن يتصف بصفات الإدراك ساقطة من (أ) و(ج)؛ على أن العبارة موجودة على هامش (أ) بخط مغاير وأثبت بالهامش على أنه شرح دون تصحيح .
(۲) في (ب) زيادة (أي: زاد).
His life, likewise the word, hearing, then sight, by [the one] who brought us the [message]...
His saying: 'His life' is coordinated with 'existence' with the deletion of the conjunction. And what the commentator did is a resolution of the meaning as previously. Al-Shaykh al-Sanusi defined life with a definition that includes both eternal and originated life: he said: 'It is an attribute that renders valid for the one in whom it subsists perception'; i.e., it renders valid for the one in whom it subsists to be qualified with the attributes of perception. And the combination of two different realities—by eternality and temporality—does not harm him, because it is a definition (rasm) not a strict definition (hadd).
And some of them defined each of them with a specific definition. He defined eternal life as: 'An eternal attribute that necessitates the validity of knowledge'; i.e., it necessitates the validity of being qualified with it, and just as it necessitates the validity of being qualified with knowledge, it necessitates the validity of being qualified with other necessary attributes. He only restricted it to knowledge because it is a condition for others, and the condition of a condition is a condition.
And he inserted the word 'validity' because life does not necessarily entail knowledge in actuality, but knowledge is obligatory for Him, Most High, due to the previous proof. As for our case, knowledge may be absent despite the presence of life, as in the insane person: he is alive while knowledge is absent from him.
And he defined originated life as: 'A quality that necessitates the acceptance of sensation and voluntary movement'; i.e., an accident that necessitates the acceptance of sensation and the acceptance of voluntary movement, unlike involuntary movement like the movement of a stone by its mover's movement. And God's life is by His essence, not a spirit, and our life is not by our essence but by means of a spirit.
And the proof of the necessity of life for Him, Most High, is that you say: God is qualified with power, will, and knowledge, and everyone who is thus must have life. So God must have life.
(1) His saying: (i.e., it renders valid for the one in whom it subsists to be qualified with the attributes of perception) is missing from (A) and (C); however, the phrase exists in the margin of (A) in a different hand and was written in the margin as an explanation without correction.
(2) In (B) there is an addition: 'i.e., he added.'
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line from the poem regarding God's attribute of life. The commentator begins by quoting the poem and then explains that 'life' is coordinated with 'existence.' He then presents al-Sanusi's definition of life, which encompasses both eternal (God's) and originated (created) life: life is an attribute that makes perception possible for the being it inheres in. The commentator notes that this is a 'rasm' (descriptive definition) not a 'hadd' (strict logical definition), so it can apply to two different realities. Next, he provides specific definitions: eternal life is an eternal attribute that necessitates the validity of knowledge (and by extension other attributes). The word 'validity' is used because life does not automatically entail actual knowledge; in creatures, one can be alive without knowledge (e.g., an insane person). Originated life is defined as a quality that inevitably involves sensation and voluntary movement. The passage also clarifies that God's life is by His essence—not by a spirit—while our life is through a spirit. Finally, the proof for the necessity of God's life is given: God has power, will, and knowledge; anything that has these attributes must have life; therefore God has life. This proof is a straightforward syllogism.

حركة إرادية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Life directly entails knowledge in all beings.
Correction: Life only makes knowledge possible (valid); in creatures, life can exist without knowledge (e.g., the insane). For God, knowledge is obligatory, but life itself does not automatically produce knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the proof that God must have the attribute of life?
A) Because life is mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because God has power, will, and knowledge, and whoever has these must have life.
C) Because all living things must have a creator.
D) Because life is necessary for sensation.

Key Takeaway
The attribute of life is necessary for God because it is a prerequisite for the attributes of power, will, and knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now understand that God's life is self-subsisting, not dependent on a spirit, while your own life is a fragile loan from Him. When you fear losing your health or your very existence, do you truly anchor your trust in the Ever-Living who never dies? What specific practice can you adopt today to remind yourself that your life is in His hands alone?
?
The proof that God must have life because He has power, will, and knowledge is rationally certain. But does your daily life reflect this certainty? In moments of weakness or decision, do you consciously turn to the Living God, relying on His power and knowledge rather than your own limited resources? What would change in your actions tomorrow if you lived with full awareness that God is alive and active in every detail?

A Comprehensive Definition of Life
Sanusi defines life generally, then gives separate definitions for eternal and temporal life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic theologians define life in a way that covers both God's eternal life and created temporal life, and why a descriptive definition (rasm) is used instead of a real definition (hadd).

Core Idea
Life makes perception possible; a single definition covers both eternal and temporal existence.

Before proving that God is alive, theologians must first define what life means. The passage presents a definition by Imam al-Sanusi that is broad enough to apply to both God and creatures, while also providing separate definitions for each. This lesson unpacks those definitions and explains the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Read the general definition of life
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noting how Shaykh al-Sanusi defines life as an attribute that makes perception correct for the one in whom it subsists. Then read the translation and commentary.
Pay attention to why this definition is called a 'rasm' (descriptive) not a 'hadd' (real).
2
Identify the two specific definitions
The commentator then gives separate definitions for eternal life (God's life) and temporal life (created life). Locate each definition and note the key differences.
Eternal life is defined as entailing the validity of knowledge; temporal life as a quality that entails sensation and voluntary movement.
3
Understand the role of 'validity' (صحة)
Notice that the definition of eternal life includes the word 'validity' (صحة). The commentator explains that life does not necessitate actual knowledge—it only makes it possible. Reflect on the example of the madman.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding about life and knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٤. صفة الحياة ودليلها]
قوله : (حَيَاتُهُ) معطوف على الوجود بحذف حرف العطف، وما صنعه الشارح حل معنى كما تقدَّم، وقد عرف الشيخ السنوسي الحياة بتعريف يشمل الحياة القديمة والحادثة؛ حيث قال: هي صفةٌ تصحُحُ لمن قامت به الإدراك؛ أي: تصحح لمن قامت به أن يتصف بصفات الإدراك ) ، ولا يضره الجمع بين حقيقتين مختلفتين بالقدم والحدوث؛ لأنَّه رسم لا حد. كلًّا وعرف بعضهم منهما بتعريف يخصه، فعرف الحياة القديمة بقوله : (صفة أزلية تقتضي صحة العلم؛ أي: تقتضي صحة الاتصاف به وكما تقتضي صحة الاتصاف بالعلم تقتضي صحة الاتصاف بغيره من الصفات الواجبة، وإنما اقتصر على العلم شرط في غيره، وشرط الشرط شرط. لأنه وأقحم (٢) لفظة (صحة) ؛ لأن الحياة لا تستلزم العلم بالفعل، لكن العلم واجب في حقه تعالى للدليل السابق وأما في حقنا فقد ينتفي العلم مع وجود الحياة، كما في المجنون؛ فإنه حي مع انتفاء العلم عنه . وعرف الحياة الحادثة بقوله : (هي كيفية يلزمها قبول الحس والحركة الإرادية)؛ أي : عَرَضُ يلزمه قبول الإحساس وقبول الحركة الإرادية، بخلاف الحركة الاضطرارية كحركة الحجر بحركة محركه، وحياة الله لذاته ليست بروح، وحياتنا ليست لذاتنا بل بسبب روح
ودليل وجوب الحياة له تعالى أن تقول : الله متصف بالقدرة والإرادة والعلم، وكلُّ من كان كذلك تجب له الحياة، فالله تجب له الحياة.
(١) قوله : (أي: تصحح لمن قامت به أن يتصف بصفات الإدراك ساقطة من (أ) و(ج)؛ على أن العبارة موجودة على هامش (أ) بخط مغاير وأثبت بالهامش على أنه شرح دون تصحيح .
(٢) في (ب) زيادة (أي: زاد).
His statement: (His life) is conjoined to existence with the omission of the conjunction, and what the commentator did is to solve the meaning as previously. Indeed, Shaykh al-Sanusi defined life with a definition that encompasses the eternal and the temporal life, when he said: It is an attribute that renders correct for the one in whom it subsists perception; that is, it renders correct for the one in whom it subsists to be described with the attributes of perception. And it does not harm him to combine two different realities in terms of pre-eternity and temporality, because it is a descriptive definition (rasm), not a real definition (hadd). Rather, some of them defined each of them with a definition specific to it. So he defined the eternal life by his saying: An eternal attribute that entails the validity of knowledge; that is, it entails the validity of being described by it. And just as it entails the validity of being described by knowledge, it entails the validity of being described by other obligatory attributes. He limited it to knowledge because it is a condition for others, and the condition of a condition is a condition. He inserted the word 'validity' because life does not necessitate actual knowledge, but knowledge is obligatory in His, exalted, case due to the previous proof. As for our case, knowledge may be absent while life exists, as in the madman, for he is alive while knowledge is absent from him. And he defined temporal life by his saying: It is a quality that entails the acceptance of sensation and voluntary movement; that is, an accident that entails the acceptance of sensation and the acceptance of voluntary movement, unlike involuntary movement like the movement of a stone by the movement of its mover. And the life of God, exalted, is not by a soul, and our life is not by itself but by means of a soul. The proof of the necessity of life for Him, exalted, is that you say: God is described with power, will, and knowledge, and everyone who is thus must have life, so God must have life. (1) His statement: (i.e., 'renders correct for the one in whom it subsists to be described with the attributes of perception') is missing from (A) and (J); however, the phrase is present in the margin of (A) in a different handwriting and is established in the margin as a commentary without correction. (2) In (B) an addition: (i.e., he added).
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line of the poem about the attribute of life. It begins by explaining the grammar of the word 'life' in the text. Then it presents the definition of life from Shaykh al-Sanusi, which is broad enough to cover both God's eternal life and created temporal life. The definition states that life is an attribute that makes perception possible for the being in whom it resides. The commentator notes that this is a descriptive definition (rasm), not a real definition (hadd), so it is acceptable that it applies to two different realities. Next, the passage gives separate definitions for eternal and temporal life. The definition of eternal life says it is an eternal attribute that entails the validity of being described with knowledge, and by extension other attributes. The insertion of the word 'validity' is important because life does not necessitate actual knowledge, as seen in the case of a mad person who is alive but lacks knowledge. The definition of temporal life says it is a quality that entails the reception of sensation and voluntary movement, an accident that makes the body capable of sensation and voluntary motion, as opposed to forced motion. Finally, the proof for God's life is presented: since God has power, will, and knowledge, and every being with these attributes must have life, God necessarily has life.

Key Terms

صفة
إدراك
رسم
حد
كيفية
عرض
روح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Life necessarily means a person has actual knowledge and awareness at all times.
Correction: The text explains that life only makes perception possible, not actual; a madman is alive but lacks knowledge. The word 'validity' (صحة) in the definition shows that life entails the potential for knowledge, not its actuality.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what does the definition of eternal life specifically entail?
A) Actual knowledge at all times
B) The validity of being described with knowledge
C) The ability to speak
D) The presence of a soul

Key Takeaway
Life is defined as an attribute that makes perception possible, and it is a descriptive definition (rasm) applicable to both God and creatures, with specific definitions highlighting the potential for knowledge and the capacity for sensation and voluntary movement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you living in a way that your life is truly enabling you to perceive the signs of Allah, or are you content to merely exist like the madman who is alive but unaware? What will you change today to sharpen your perception?
?
If your life is only a quality that entails sensation and voluntary movement, what are you voluntarily moving toward? Is it the pleasure of Allah or the gratification of your own desires?
?
You have learned that God's life is not through a soul, but yours is. Does this realization humble you to recognize your dependency on Allah for even your existence? How will you express this dependency in your worship today?

The Proof for God's Life
A concise syllogistic proof that God must have life because He has power, will, and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that God must possess the attribute of life based on His other attributes of power, will, and knowledge.

Core Idea
Where there is power, will, and knowledge, life must be present.

Having defined life, the commentator now provides a concise proof that God is necessarily alive. The argument is straightforward: God has power, will, and knowledge, and any being with these attributes must have life. This lesson examines the logic of this proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof sentence in Arabic
Read the Arabic text of the proof slowly. It is a single sentence that contains a logical argument. Make sure you understand each part.
The proof is structured as a syllogism with a major premise, minor premise, and conclusion.
2
Break down the syllogism
Identify the three parts: the major premise (every being with power, will, and knowledge must have life), the minor premise (God is described with power, will, and knowledge), and the conclusion (God must have life).
This is a standard form of proof in kalam.
3
Reflect on the logic
Consider why the major premise is true. The earlier definitions of life show that life makes perception possible, and power, will, and knowledge are attributes of perception. So life is a necessary prerequisite for these attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

The Sunni Doctrine of God's Speech
Sunni definition of God's speech as eternal and non-composite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, not composed of letters or sounds.

Core Idea
God's speech is an eternal attribute, not letters or sounds.

The passage presents the Sunni doctrine of God's speech in contrast to other sects. Here we focus on the positive definition: what Sunni scholars affirm about this divine attribute. The definition is precise and negates any composition or temporal characteristics.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sunni definition
Read the Arabic passage where the Sunni position is stated: 'صفةٌ أزليةٌ قائمة بذاته تعالى ليست بحرف ولا صوت...'
Notice the sequence of negations and affirmations.
2
Identify the key negations
Find what God's speech is not: not a letter, not a sound, not subject to temporal features like anteriority/posteriority, inflection, etc.
These negations protect God's transcendence.
3
Understand the affirmations
It is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, free from psychological silence and internal defects.
This distinguishes it from human speech.
4
Compare with other attributes
The passage says speech is like the preceding attributes in obligatoriness but differs in proof. Reflect on the uniqueness of speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٥. صفة الكلام ودليلها]
قوله : (كَذَا الكَلامُ ) ( كذا) خبرٌ ،مقدَّم ، و (الكلام) مبتدأ مؤخر، والمعنى: الكلام مثل ذا ؛ أي مثل ما تقدم من الصفات والتشبيه ليس من كل وجه بل في مطلق الوجوب الله تعالى وإن خالفها في الدليل؛ لأنَّ دليلها عقلي؛ إما وحده، وإما مع النقلي على وجه التأكيد، ودليله نقلي إما وحده أو مع العقلي(١) على وجه التأكيد؛ فالمعول عليه فيه الدليل السمعي كما سيذكره بقوله : (بذي أتانا السمع). وقد اختلف أهل الملل والمذاهب في معنى كلامه تعالى، فقال أهل السنة : صفةٌ أزليةٌ قائمة بذاته تعالى ليست بحرف ولا صوت منزهة عن التقدم والتأخر والإعراب والبناء، ومنزهة عن السكوت النفسي بألا يدبر في نفسه الكلام مع القدرة عليه، ومنزهةً عن الآفة الباطنية بألا يقدر على ذلك والطفولية. ا في حال الخرس وقالت الحشوية وطائفةٌ سموا أنفسهم بالحنابلة كلامه تعالى هو الحروف والأصواتُ المتوالية المترتبةُ ، ويزعمون أنها قديمة، وتغالى بعضُهم حتى زعم قدم هذه الحروف التي نقرؤها والرسوم، بل تجاوز جهلُ بعضهم لغلافِ المصحف (٣) .
(١) قوله : (إما وحده أو مع العقلي معناه أنك بالخيار بين أن تستدل بالدليل النقلي وتقتصر عليه، وبين أن تضم إليه الدليل العقلي للتأكيد والتقوية، وهو ما ذكره السنوسي بقوله: (وأيضاً لو لم يتصف بها لزم أن يتصف بأضدادها وهي نقائص والنقص عليه تعالى محال). انتهى أجهوري.
(٢) قوله : (كما في حال الخرس إلخ) التشبيه في مطلق الآفة، وإن كانت الآفة المشبهة هي الآفة الباطنية المانعة من الكلام النفسي والآفة المشبهة بها وهي الخرس، والطفولية ظاهرية مانعة من الكلام اللفظي . انتهى أجهوري.
(٣) قال الإمام السنوسي في شرح الكبرى ( ص ٢٦٧) : (وبالجملة فاعتقاد الحشوية تألف من ضلالات ثلاث : : من تهود وتنصُّر واعتزال ؛ فهم مع اليهود في اعتقادهم الجسم في حق الله، ومع النصارى في اعتقاد حلول الكلام في الأجسام، وأنه لا يفارق مع ذلك الإله، ومع المعتزلة في اعتقاد أن كلام الله تعالى حروف وأصوات، وهو نص مذهب اليهود أيضاً، غير أن المعتزلة لم يقولوا بقيام الحروف والأصوات به سبحانه وتعالى لما تفطنوا لحدوثها، وأدركوا أن قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى محال، وهؤلاء حكموا بذلك لعظيم غباوتهم وجهلهم الضروريات التي تدرك بأوائل العقول، واشترك الجميع في عدم تعقل ما قاله أهل الحق من إثبات كلام ليس بحرف ولا صوت قائم بنفس المتكلم، يعبر عنه بالكلام اللفظي والكتابة والرموز والإشارات).
[5. The Attribute of Speech and Its Proof]
His statement: (Thus speech) – (Thus) is a predicate placed before, and (speech) is the subject placed after, and the meaning is: speech is like this; that is, like the preceding attributes, and the comparison is not in every respect but in the absolute obligatoriness for God, exalted, even if it differs from them in the proof. Because their proof is rational, either alone or with the transmitted as an emphasis, and its proof is transmitted either alone or with the rational as an emphasis; so reliance is placed upon the transmitted proof as he will mention by his saying: (With which the hearing brought us). And the people of religions and sects differed concerning the meaning of His, exalted, speech. The People of the Sunna said: an eternal attribute subsisting in His, exalted, essence, not a letter or a sound, transcendent of anteriority and posteriority, inflection and declension, and transcendent of psychological silence such that He does not deliberate speech in Himself while being able to do so, and transcendent of the internal defect such that He is not able to do that and childishness in the case of dumbness. And the Hashwiyya and a group who call themselves Hanabila said: His, exalted, speech is the consecutive ordered letters and sounds, and they claim they are eternal, and some of them exaggerated until they claimed the eternity of these letters we recite and the scripts, rather the ignorance of some of them exceeded to the cover of the Quran. (1) His statement: (either alone or with the rational) means that you have the choice between deducing with the transmitted proof and limiting yourself to it, and between adding to it the rational proof for emphasis and strengthening, and this is what al-Sanusi mentioned in his saying: (Also, if He were not described with it, He would have to be described with their opposites, which are deficiencies, and deficiency is impossible for Him, exalted). End of al-Ujhuri. (2) His statement: (as in the case of dumbness etc.) the comparison is in the absolute defect, although the defect compared is the internal defect preventing psychological speech, and that which it is compared to is dumbness, and childishness is external preventing verbal speech. End of al-Ujhuri. (3) Imam al-Sanusi said in his commentary on al-Kubra (p. 267): (In summary, the belief of the Hashwiyya is composed of three misguidances: from Judaism, Christianity, and Mu'tazilism. They are with the Jews in their belief in the body for God, with the Christians in their belief in the indwelling of speech in bodies and that it does not separate from the divine, and with the Mu'tazila in their belief that the speech of God, exalted, is letters and sounds, and this is also the explicit doctrine of the Jews, except that the Mu'tazila did not say that letters and sounds subsist in Him, exalted, because they realized they are originated and understood that the subsistence of originated things in His essence is impossible. These people judged this due to their great stupidity and ignorance of necessary things perceived by primary intellects. And all shared in not comprehending what the People of Truth said of affirming speech that is not a letter nor a sound, subsisting in the speaker, expressed by verbal speech, writing, symbols, and indications.)
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line of the poem about the attribute of speech. It begins by explaining the grammar of the word 'speech' in the text. The comparison of speech to the preceding attributes is not in every respect but in the absolute necessity of the attribute for God. The proof for speech is primarily transmitted, though a rational proof can be added for emphasis. Then the passage presents the Sunni doctrine: God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, not composed of letters or sounds, transcendent of temporal features and defects. It then contrasts this with the views of the Hashwiyya and self-proclaimed Hanabila, who believe God's speech is literal letters and sounds that are eternal, some even claiming the letters we recite and the physical Quran cover are eternal. The footnotes elaborate: the rational proof for speech (that denying it implies deficiencies) comes from Sanusi; the comparison with dumbness is explained; and a longer footnote from Sanusi's Sharh al-Kubra classifies the Hashwiyya belief as a combination of Jewish, Christian, and Mu'tazilite errors, noting that the Mu'tazila at least avoided attributing originated letters to God, unlike the Hashwiyya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's speech is composed of letters and sounds like human speech.
Correction: The text explicitly says it is 'not a letter or sound' (ليست بحرف ولا صوت) and is an eternal attribute, not a temporal sequence.

Checkpoint
According to the Sunni definition in the text, what is God's speech?
A) A creation that appears at will
B) An eternal attribute not composed of letters or sounds
C) An attribute that changes over time
D) The Quran written in Arabic

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal, non-composite attribute subsisting in His essence, free from all temporal and compositional defects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you truly believe you are uttering God's eternal speech, not a created thing? How would your reverence change if you fully internalized that every letter you read is an expression of an uncreated attribute?
?
The passage says God's speech is transcendent of anteriority and posteriority. Does your faith sometimes imagine God's words as sequential—first the Torah, then the Gospel, then the Qur'an? How can this truth help you trust that all His words are equally present and real for you today?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
4 min
The Proof for God's Speech
Discussion of the proof for God's speech as primarily transmitted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of speech is proven primarily by transmitted evidence (scripture) and how rational proof can support it.

Core Idea
Speech is proven by revelation, with reason as an emphatic support.

The commentary explains that speech differs from other attributes: while others like knowledge and power are proven by reason, speech relies on the transmitted proof (the Quran and Hadith). A rational proof can be added for emphasis, but the primary evidence is scriptural.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on proof
Read the Arabic passage where the author discusses the proof for speech and its relation to other attributes.
2
Identify the two types of proof
Note the distinction: rational (عقلي) and transmitted (نقلي). For speech, the transmitted is primary, though rational can be used for emphasis.
The author says 'أما وحده أو مع العقلي على وجه التأكيد'.
3
Understand the unique nature of speech
The reason for relying on transmitted proof is that speech is not directly deducible by reason alone; we need revelation to know that God speaks.
This is unlike attributes like power, which reason can deduce.
4
See the rational proof from Sanusi
The footnote provides the rational proof: if God were not described with speech, He would be described with its opposite (silence/inability), which is a deficiency, and deficiency is impossible for God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٥. صفة الكلام ودليلها]
قوله : (كَذَا الكَلامُ ) ( كذا) خبرٌ ،مقدَّم ، و (الكلام) مبتدأ مؤخر، والمعنى: الكلام مثل ذا ؛ أي مثل ما تقدم من الصفات والتشبيه ليس من كل وجه بل في مطلق الوجوب الله تعالى وإن خالفها في الدليل؛ لأنَّ دليلها عقلي؛ إما وحده، وإما مع النقلي على وجه التأكيد، ودليله نقلي إما وحده أو مع العقلي(١) على وجه التأكيد؛ فالمعول عليه فيه الدليل السمعي كما سيذكره بقوله : (بذي أتانا السمع). وقد اختلف أهل الملل والمذاهب في معنى كلامه تعالى، فقال أهل السنة : صفةٌ أزليةٌ قائمة بذاته تعالى ليست بحرف ولا صوت منزهة عن التقدم والتأخر والإعراب والبناء، ومنزهة عن السكوت النفسي بألا يدبر في نفسه الكلام مع القدرة عليه، ومنزهةً عن الآفة الباطنية بألا يقدر على ذلك والطفولية. ا في حال الخرس وقالت الحشوية وطائفةٌ سموا أنفسهم بالحنابلة كلامه تعالى هو الحروف والأصواتُ المتوالية المترتبةُ ، ويزعمون أنها قديمة، وتغالى بعضُهم حتى زعم قدم هذه الحروف التي نقرؤها والرسوم، بل تجاوز جهلُ بعضهم لغلافِ المصحف (٣) .
(١) قوله : (إما وحده أو مع العقلي معناه أنك بالخيار بين أن تستدل بالدليل النقلي وتقتصر عليه، وبين أن تضم إليه الدليل العقلي للتأكيد والتقوية، وهو ما ذكره السنوسي بقوله: (وأيضاً لو لم يتصف بها لزم أن يتصف بأضدادها وهي نقائص والنقص عليه تعالى محال). انتهى أجهوري.
(٢) قوله : (كما في حال الخرس إلخ) التشبيه في مطلق الآفة، وإن كانت الآفة المشبهة هي الآفة الباطنية المانعة من الكلام النفسي والآفة المشبهة بها وهي الخرس، والطفولية ظاهرية مانعة من الكلام اللفظي . انتهى أجهوري.
(٣) قال الإمام السنوسي في شرح الكبرى ( ص ٢٦٧) : (وبالجملة فاعتقاد الحشوية تألف من ضلالات ثلاث : : من تهود وتنصُّر واعتزال ؛ فهم مع اليهود في اعتقادهم الجسم في حق الله، ومع النصارى في اعتقاد حلول الكلام في الأجسام، وأنه لا يفارق مع ذلك الإله، ومع المعتزلة في اعتقاد أن كلام الله تعالى حروف وأصوات، وهو نص مذهب اليهود أيضاً، غير أن المعتزلة لم يقولوا بقيام الحروف والأصوات به سبحانه وتعالى لما تفطنوا لحدوثها، وأدركوا أن قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى محال، وهؤلاء حكموا بذلك لعظيم غباوتهم وجهلهم الضروريات التي تدرك بأوائل العقول، واشترك الجميع في عدم تعقل ما قاله أهل الحق من إثبات كلام ليس بحرف ولا صوت قائم بنفس المتكلم، يعبر عنه بالكلام اللفظي والكتابة والرموز والإشارات).
[5. The Attribute of Speech and Its Proof]
His statement: (Thus speech) – (Thus) is a predicate placed before, and (speech) is the subject placed after, and the meaning is: speech is like this; that is, like the preceding attributes, and the comparison is not in every respect but in the absolute obligatoriness for God, exalted, even if it differs from them in the proof. Because their proof is rational, either alone or with the transmitted as an emphasis, and its proof is transmitted either alone or with the rational as an emphasis; so reliance is placed upon the transmitted proof as he will mention by his saying: (With which the hearing brought us). And the people of religions and sects differed concerning the meaning of His, exalted, speech. The People of the Sunna said: an eternal attribute subsisting in His, exalted, essence, not a letter or a sound, transcendent of anteriority and posteriority, inflection and declension, and transcendent of psychological silence such that He does not deliberate speech in Himself while being able to do so, and transcendent of the internal defect such that He is not able to do that and childishness in the case of dumbness. And the Hashwiyya and a group who call themselves Hanabila said: His, exalted, speech is the consecutive ordered letters and sounds, and they claim they are eternal, and some of them exaggerated until they claimed the eternity of these letters we recite and the scripts, rather the ignorance of some of them exceeded to the cover of the Quran. (1) His statement: (either alone or with the rational) means that you have the choice between deducing with the transmitted proof and limiting yourself to it, and between adding to it the rational proof for emphasis and strengthening, and this is what al-Sanusi mentioned in his saying: (Also, if He were not described with it, He would have to be described with their opposites, which are deficiencies, and deficiency is impossible for Him, exalted). End of al-Ujhuri. (2) His statement: (as in the case of dumbness etc.) the comparison is in the absolute defect, although the defect compared is the internal defect preventing psychological speech, and that which it is compared to is dumbness, and childishness is external preventing verbal speech. End of al-Ujhuri. (3) Imam al-Sanusi said in his commentary on al-Kubra (p. 267): (In summary, the belief of the Hashwiyya is composed of three misguidances: from Judaism, Christianity, and Mu'tazilism. They are with the Jews in their belief in the body for God, with the Christians in their belief in the indwelling of speech in bodies and that it does not separate from the divine, and with the Mu'tazila in their belief that the speech of God, exalted, is letters and sounds, and this is also the explicit doctrine of the Jews, except that the Mu'tazila did not say that letters and sounds subsist in Him, exalted, because they realized they are originated and understood that the subsistence of originated things in His essence is impossible. These people judged this due to their great stupidity and ignorance of necessary things perceived by primary intellects. And all shared in not comprehending what the People of Truth said of affirming speech that is not a letter nor a sound, subsisting in the speaker, expressed by verbal speech, writing, symbols, and indications.)
Source pages p. 178

The proof for speech is primarily transmitted, though a rational proof can be added for emphasis. Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof for the attribute of speech?
A) Rational proof alone
B) Transmitted proof (scripture)
C) Empirical observation

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly internalize it as the very speech of God, or does it become just words you repeat? What would change in your recitation today if you were absolutely certain you were hearing God speak directly to you?
?
This lesson teaches that the primary proof for God's speech is revelation, not reason. Yet how often do you demand rational explanations for matters of faith before you submit? Are there areas of your deen where you have secretly required 'proofs' that God did not provide? Will you repent of that arrogance today?
?
If God's speech (the Quran) is the foundation of your faith, but you spend more time seeking intellectual arguments for it than actually living by it, what does that reveal about the state of your heart? What is one concrete change you will make this week to prioritize submission over speculation?
